# What Happens Below 1 sat/vB + The Hidden Risks of Sub-1 sat/vB Bitcoin Transactions | UniSat

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/articles/understanding-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions/what-happens-below-1-sat-vb-+-the-hidden-risks-of-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions#what-happens-when-bitcoin-fee-rates-drop-below-1-sat-vb)

**What Happens When Bitcoin Fee Rates Drop Below 1 sat/vB?**

Bitcoin transaction fees are measured in **satoshis per virtual byte (sat/vB)**. This unit helps miners prioritize transactions when adding blocks to the blockchain. Bitcoin's **default relay policy** (followed by most nodes) requires a minimum fee rate of **1 sat/vB** for a transaction to be relayed across the network. This policy exists to:

1.  Provide a minimum economic incentive for miners to include transactions.
    
2.  Prevent spam by making it costly to flood the network.
    
3.  Maintain efficient network operation by limiting mempool bloat.
    

Transactions paying **less than 1 sat/vB** (sub-1 sat/vB) are considered **non-standard** under this default policy.

However, as the ecosystem evolves there may be some demand for sub-1 sat/vB transactions and more occasions where the miner may accept these transactions such as when the mempool cleared recently.So how do these sub-1 sat/vB transactions work?

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/articles/understanding-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions/what-happens-below-1-sat-vb-+-the-hidden-risks-of-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions#when-can-sub-1-sat-vb-transactions-be-confirmed)

**⏳ When Can Sub-1 sat/vB Transactions Be Confirmed?**

*   **Not Relayed:** They are **not broadcast or relayed** by nodes enforcing the default policy. They will **not enter the public mempool**.
    
*   **Confirmation only possible** if:
    
    *   The transaction is **submitted directly to a miner** (bypassing the public peer-to-peer network), _or_
        
    *   The transaction is submitted via a **private relay service** (like Slipstream used by some pools) that accepts sub-1 sat/vB rates, _or_
        
    
*   **Not Guaranteed:** Even if directly submitted to a miner or pool, **inclusion is never guaranteed**.
    

Miners prioritize transactions based on their own fee thresholds and strategies. Sub-1 sat/vB transactions are the lowest priority and will only be mined when there is plenty of unused block space and the individual miner or mining pool explicitly chooses to accept and mine sub-1 sat/vB transactions using custom mempool policies.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/articles/understanding-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions/what-happens-below-1-sat-vb-+-the-hidden-risks-of-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions#potential-benefits-of-sub-1-sat-vb-transactions)

**💡 Potential Benefits of Sub-1 sat/vB Transactions**

*   **Lower Costs:** _If confirmed_, they enable cheaper transactions, potentially benefiting low-value transfers or microtransactions. (It wouldn’t make sense if you want send $1 worth of BTC but have to spend $5 on gas right)
    
*   **Reduced Minting Costs:** Protocols relying heavily on on-chain transactions for operations like minting (e.g., Runes, Ordinals, brc-20 tickers) could see significant cost reductions.
    

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/articles/understanding-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions/what-happens-below-1-sat-vb-+-the-hidden-risks-of-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions#the-hidden-risks-of-sub-1-sat-vb-transactions)

The Hidden Risks of Sub-1 sat/vB Transactions

#1 Stuck Transactions:

*   Most mining pools currently **do not mine** transactions with 0.1 sat/vB or similar ultra-low fee rates
    
*   Your transaction may remain **unconfirmed for days, weeks, or indefinitely**
    
*   **Funds become inaccessible** - you can't spend the same UTXOs until the transaction confirms
    
*   **P**articularly problematic for time-sensitive operations such as mint or trade
    

#2 Dust UTXO Attacks

**How the Attack Works:**

*   **Malicious actors** send low-fee-rate UTXOs to your address
    
*   Later, your wallet automatically includes this UTXO when constructing a new transaction
    
*   The **entire transaction inherits the low fee rate**, making it unconfirmable
    
*   You must pay expensive RBF (Replace-By-Fee) acceleration costs to fix the issue
    
*   Why it’s sneaky:
    
    *   Our wallet blocks UTXOs <600 sats, but attacks over 600 sats bypass this.
        
    *   Merging these UTXOs (via wallet tools) spreads the poison to new transactions.
        
    

#3: Transaction Chain Limitations

**The Technical Problem:**

*   Bitcoin's mempool has a **25-transaction ancestor limit**
    
*   Repeatedly spending 0.1 sat/vB transactions quickly approaches this limit
    
*   Once reached, **new transactions cannot be broadcast**
    
*   Regular users have **no way to resolve this** without technical tools
    

**Resolution Challenges:**

*   **Only solution** is using RBF (Replace-By-Fee) acceleration tools to replace earlier transactions
    
*   **Current tool limitations** - many RBF implementations have bugs and don't handle data cleanup properly
    

#4: Increased Spam Transactions:

Lowering the _effective_ cost barrier significantly makes it cheaper for attackers to flood the network with spam or dust transactions (very small outputs), potentially disrupting normal operation.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/articles/understanding-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions/what-happens-below-1-sat-vb-+-the-hidden-risks-of-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions#recommendations-for-users)

🎯 Recommendations for Users

*   Avoid sub-1 sat/vB transactions unless you fully understand the risks
    
*   Be Aware of the limited ecosystem support for handling sub-1 sat/vB transactions properly and potential inconsistent behavior across different wallet implementations
    
*   Keep RBF tools available for emergency acceleration
    
*   We recommend checking the current Bitcoin network congestion. A fee rate of 1 sat/vB or lower means it may result in longer confirmation times. You may use [mempool.spacearrow-up-right](https://mempool.space/)
     to view the fee rate and estimated confirmation time in real time.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252F8cxLuXVdC63zPNw4L3uq%252F88.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D6d40893d-acdc-4c3a-939f-dde0a5efeba1&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=9b5462cc&sv=2)

**Disclaimer:**

The content of this document is for informational purposes only. # Understanding Bitcoin Address Types | UniSat

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/knowledge-base/bitcoin/understanding-bitcoin-address-types#id-1.-legacy)

1\. **Legacy**


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   Legacy transactions, also known as Pay-to-Public-Key-Hash (P2PKH), represent the original and most common address format.
    
*   Addresses in this format start with the number "1."
    
*   Legacy transactions are less space-efficient and can lead to higher transaction fees due to their larger size.
    

Example Legacy Address: `1A1zP1eP5QGefi2DMPTfTL5SLmv7DivfNa`

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/knowledge-base/bitcoin/understanding-bitcoin-address-types#id-2.-nested-segwit-p2sh-p2wpkh)

**2\. Nested SegWit (P2SH-P2WPKH)**


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   Nested SegWit, or Pay-to-Witness-Public-Key-Hash (P2SH-P2WPKH), is an interim solution that combines features of both Legacy and Native SegWit.
    
*   Addresses in this format start with the number "3."
    
*   It allows Legacy wallets to send funds to SegWit addresses while still benefiting from lower fees.
    

Example Nested SegWit Address: `3J98t1WpEZ73CNmQviecrnyiWrnqRhWNLy`

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/knowledge-base/bitcoin/understanding-bitcoin-address-types#id-3.-native-segwit-bech32)

**3\. Native SegWit (bech32)**


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   Native SegWit, or bech32, represents an improvement over Legacy transactions in terms of scalability and reduced transaction fees.
    
*   Addresses in this format start with "bc1."
    
*   Native SegWit uses a more efficient scripting language (Segregated Witness) to reduce transaction size.
    

Example Native SegWit Address: `bc1qar0srrr7xfkvy5l643lydnw9re59gtzzwf5mdq`

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/knowledge-base/bitcoin/understanding-bitcoin-address-types#id-4.-taproot)

**4\. Taproot**


------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   Taproot is the latest Bitcoin address format designed to enhance privacy, scalability, and scripting capabilities. Addresses in this format start with "bc1p."
    
*   Taproot allows the aggregation of multiple signatures, making complex transactions more efficient and cost-effective.
    

Example Taproot Address: `bc1puaz84y65g0jh7zlhwv9vwhuu3se8ldf82lk5ca6zru6kdny2zvws69x6jd`

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/knowledge-base/bitcoin/understanding-bitcoin-address-types#our-recommendation)

Our recommendation


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

For UniSat Wallet users, we suggest choosing Taproot or Native Segwit. Taproot offers substantial cost savings on transaction fees, but not all CEX platforms support it. Native SegWit has better compatibility with CEX platforms.

**Disclaimer:**

The content of this document is for informational purposes only. It does not constitute (i) investment advice or recommendations, (ii) an offer, solicitation, or inducement to purchase, sell, or hold digital assets, or (iii) financial, accounting, legal, or tax advice. Digital assets (including FTs and NFTs) are subject to market volatility, involve high risk, regulatory changes, and may depreciate in value. The information is provided "as is," and we make no warranties regarding its accuracy. Please consult your legal, tax, or investment professionals to determine whether trading or holding digital assets is suitable for you.

# Transfer brc-20 in UniSat Wallet (2023) | UniSat

UniSat Wallet now supports TRANSFER of brc-20 since 1.1.15. (available here: [Google Chrome Storearrow-up-right](https://chrome.google.com/webstore/detail/ppbibelpcjmhbdihakflkdcoccbgbkpo)
)

Please follow the step-by-step guide below to learn how to transfer your brc-20 to others.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/articles/transfer-brc-20-in-unisat-wallet-2023#id-3af9)

1\. Make sure the version of Unisat is the latest.

*   Switch to the 'Settings' tab and scroll to the bottom.
    
*   Verify the version number to make sure it’s the latest, current is **1.4.5 .**
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FcuPiVtMDN31DytmNmW49%252F1.PNG%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dbde17c96-9d6e-4a9b-9703-05013252b54e&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=82953930&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/articles/transfer-brc-20-in-unisat-wallet-2023#id-6bcf)

2\. Switch to the ‘Home’ tab and click the ‘brc-20’ tag

Each volumn here represents a specific brc-20 tick (like ‘sats’), containing multiple associated inscriptions.Please note that the balance contains two parts:

*   **Transferable**: The amount here has been inscribed into one or more TRANSFER inscriptions (can be transferred immediately).
    
*   **Available**: The amount here is available as a part of your balance (including both minted and received) **but not transferable yet**. To spend it, you must first inscribe a certain amount into a TRANSFER inscription.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FOJRNNpJgCGwt06cLYW2C%252F2.PNG%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D0deccf4e-0183-4c3d-9149-50265e49ad18&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=e53599fc&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/articles/transfer-brc-20-in-unisat-wallet-2023#e624)

3\. Click one of your brc-20s to check out the details.

*   All your associated inscriptions are listed here.
    
*   The green ones are transferable (please note we have no transferable inscription yet on the screenshot below).
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252F7CPypJ1ssguvIbGMHW5c%252F3.PNG%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Deb37627e-2234-4998-b57a-0a52237e22e3&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=b27a42a3&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/articles/transfer-brc-20-in-unisat-wallet-2023#id-33b2)

4\. Click ‘TRANSFER’ to enter the transfer process.

*   All transferable inscriptions are listed here for you to choose from.
    
*   The transfer Amount is not an editable field. It can only be calculated by the sum of the chosen amounts of TRANSFER inscriptions.
    
*   If you don’t have enough transferable inscriptions yet, you are going to inscribe them first.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FKBjawFIcRl3jn9ic2tsQ%252F5.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Deb9dc8e6-3299-42ca-beac-2303a138833b&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=8a548979&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/articles/transfer-brc-20-in-unisat-wallet-2023#id-85eb)

5\. Click the ‘Inscribe TRANSFER’ button.

*   Input the amount that you want to inscribe into a TRANSFER inscription.
    
*   Choose an appropriate fee rate.
    
*   And click the ‘Inscribe TRANSFER’ button on the bottom.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FvmTTTK9K0rNLmwfHNCfn%252F6.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D8157dae1-6446-4ac8-bc73-0ec89e9e7f48&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=acc9baf3&sv=2)

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/articles/transfer-brc-20-in-unisat-wallet-2023#e3b8)

6\. Preview the details of the TRANSFER inscription and click ‘Pay & Inscribe’ to execute

*   You may return to the earlier steps by clicking the back button and changing values and settings before submitting.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FHdnT6vYYn3AOF6Tk9Fif%252F7.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dd114b993-d461-40e6-90f0-52704a826d7d&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=4a0dffb9&sv=2)

Preview TRANSFER

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FZTZlJCXy7PyxltvRI3iX%252F8.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3c9ca91c-24aa-4df9-8364-a641452bb39b&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=7a099d78&sv=2)

Sign & Pay for transfer

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/articles/transfer-brc-20-in-unisat-wallet-2023#a257)

7\. Choose a TRANSFER inscription and proceed to step 2

*   Once a number of TRANSFER inscriptions are chosen, we can proceed to send them to the receiver by typing its address (or .sats name)
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252F3Beh3SQQipQEuJT39IYw%252F9.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dc37edd8e-65d2-46b8-b0f4-809d5f62f382&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=7dc6b66d&sv=2)

Choose TRANSFER and click ‘Next’

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FLkY4K9e7mNRpJGvyzSM9%252F10.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3993f5b0-0633-4b2f-9b26-49cb6656743a&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=738a27d7&sv=2)

Input the address or .unisat name of the receiver

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/articles/transfer-brc-20-in-unisat-wallet-2023#id-0c70)

*   Click ‘Sign & Send’ to perform the transfer operation eventually.

# How to Trade Alkanes on UniSat Marketplace | UniSat

This guide provides detailed instructions on how to trade Alkanes on the UniSat Marketplace. Please conduct your own research before trading. This guide is for informational purposes only and does not constitute financial advice.

* * *

**Alkanes Trading Fees on UniSat:**

*   **Buying:** 1.2% service fee
    
*   **Selling:** No service fee
    
*   **Orders below 250,000 sats:** 0% fee (for both buy & sell)
    

* * *

1.  #### 
    
    [hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/knowledge-base/alkanes/how-to-trade-alkanes-on-unisat-marketplace#connect-your-wallet)
    
    Connect Your Wallet
    

Visit [https://unisat.io/marketarrow-up-right](https://unisat.io/market)
 and connect your UniSat Wallet. You’ll find the **Alkanes Marketplace section** right on the homepage.

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FG8iWncYpVGkahdNTsgzK%252F11.PNG%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D6ca717b8-83ce-47b3-9ae6-c34e0ab26518&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=12e5be92&sv=2)

1.  #### 
    
    [hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/knowledge-base/alkanes/how-to-trade-alkanes-on-unisat-marketplace#browse-alkanes-assets)
    
    Browse Alkanes Assets
    

Select the Alkanes assets you wish to trade, or use the Search bar to find assets by name or ID. On the assets detail page:

*   Top left: View Volume, Market Cap, Holders, and Transactions...
    
*   Top right: Ticker’s K-Chart.
    
*   Bottom: All order listings related to that asset.

Choose the quantity and price you want, then click **Buy** under a specific order.

Enable the **Batch Buy** toggle in the lower-left corner of the interface and proceed with bulk selection.

    [hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/knowledge-base/alkanes/how-to-trade-alkanes-on-unisat-marketplace#sell-alkanes)

You can list your Alkanes via the **My Assets** tab.

**🔹 To List Alkanes:**

*   Go to **My Assets**
    
*   Click **List** beside the Alkanes assets you wish to sell
    
*   Enter the quantity and price, then click List items for sale

# The Hidden Risks of Sub-1 sat/vB Transactions | UniSat

While sub-1 sat/vB transactions might seem appealing due to lower fees, they introduce serious risks that every user should understand before using them. These risks can lead to stuck transactions, financial losses, and poor user experience.

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/articles/understanding-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions/the-hidden-risks-of-sub-1-sat-vb-transactions#id-1-stuck-transactions)

#1 Stuck Transactions:


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   Most mining pools currently **do not mine** transactions with 0.1 sat/vB or similar ultra-low fee rates
    
*   Your transaction may remain **unconfirmed for days, weeks, or indefinitely**
    
*   **Funds become inaccessible** - you can't spend the same UTXOs until the transaction confirms
    
*   **P**articularly problematic for time-sensitive operations such as mint or trade
    

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/articles/understanding-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions/the-hidden-risks-of-sub-1-sat-vb-transactions#id-2-dust-utxo-attacks)

#2 Dust UTXO Attacks


----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**How the Attack Works:**

*   **Malicious actors** send low-fee-rate UTXOs to your address
    
*   Later, your wallet automatically includes this UTXO when constructing a new transaction
    
*   The **entire transaction inherits the low fee rate**, making it unconfirmable
    
*   You must pay expensive RBF (Replace-By-Fee) acceleration costs to fix the issue
    
*   Why it’s sneaky:
    
    *   Our wallet blocks UTXOs <600 sats, but attacks over 600 sats bypass this.
        
    *   Merging these UTXOs (via wallet tools) spreads the poison to new transactions.
        
    

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/articles/understanding-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions/the-hidden-risks-of-sub-1-sat-vb-transactions#id-3-transaction-chain-limitations)

#3: Transaction Chain Limitations

**The Technical Problem:**

*   Bitcoin's mempool has a **25-transaction ancestor limit**
    
*   Repeatedly spending 0.1 sat/vB transactions quickly approaches this limit
    
*   Once reached, **new transactions cannot be broadcast**
    
*   Regular users have **no way to resolve this** without technical tools
    

**Resolution Challenges:**

*   **Only solution** is using RBF (Replace-By-Fee) acceleration tools to replace earlier transactions
    
*   **Current tool limitations** - many RBF implementations have bugs and don't handle data cleanup properly
    

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/articles/understanding-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions/the-hidden-risks-of-sub-1-sat-vb-transactions#recommendations-for-users)

🎯 Recommendations for Users

*   **Avoid sub-1 sat/vB transactions** unless you fully understand the risks
    
*   **Be Aware of the limited ecosystem support** for handling sub-1 sat/vB transactions properly and potential i**nconsistent behavior** across different wallet implementations
    
*   **Keep RBF tools available for emergency acceleration**
    

**How UniSat may support sub-1 sat/vB transactions**

*   We will do more research and aim to first implement in our explorer UniScan
    
*   More experimental tools may be possible in the future
    

More on how Sub-1 sat/vB transactions work: [https://docs.unisat.io/technical/understanding-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactionsarrow-up-right](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/understanding-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions)

**Disclaimer:**

The content of this document is for informational purposes only. It does not constitute (i) investment advice or recommendations, (ii) an offer, solicitation, or inducement to purchase, sell, or hold digital assets, or (iii) financial, accounting, legal, or tax advice. Digital assets (including FTs and NFTs) are subject to market volatility, involve high risk, regulatory changes, and may depreciate in value. The information is provided "as is," and we make no warranties regarding its accuracy. Please consult your legal, tax, or investment professionals to determine whether trading or holding digital assets is suitable for you.

# Understanding Sub-1 sat/vB Bitcoin Transactions | UniSat

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/articles/understanding-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions#what-is-sat-vb-and-why-is-it-important)

What is "sat/vB" and why is it important?

In the Bitcoin network, every transaction takes up space in a block, measured in **virtual bytes (vB), and t**ransaction fees are paid using **satoshis (sat), therefore the network fee rate is satoshi per virtual byte (sat/vB)**.

Node operators would prioritize confirming transactions offering higher fees (more sat per vB).

*   Higher fee rate → Faster confirmation
    
*   Lower fee rate → Delayed confirmation, or potentially never confirmed
    

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/articles/understanding-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions#why-do-most-bitcoin-nodes-require-fees-above-1-sat-vb)

Why Do Most Bitcoin Nodes Require fees above 1 sat/vB?

Bitcoin Core enforces a default minimum relay fee policy, which only accepts and relays transactions with ≥ 1 sat/vB. Most nodes follow this rule to:

1.  Ensure miner rewards
    
2.  Discourage transaction spam
    
3.  Maintain efficient mempool operation
    

This 1 sat/vB threshold has become a network-wide consensus rule. However, it is is more of a policy and not a protocol constraint.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/articles/understanding-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions#how-sub-1-sat-vb-transactions-can-be-processed)

**How Sub 1 sat/vB Transactions Can Be Processed**

Given the default minimum relay fee policy of 1 sat/vB, **Sub-1 sat/vB transaction can only be processed through:**

*   Direct submission to miners, _or_
    
*   Private relay services (e.g., Slipstream).
    

This means that confirmation of these transactions is not guaranteed, and only occurs during when network is less congested AND _if_ miners accept sub-1 sat policies.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/articles/understanding-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions#when-sub-1-sat-vb-may-be-appropriate)

✅ When Sub-1 sat/vB May Be Appropriate:

*   When the mempool is completely empty and competition is low
    
*   For non-urgent, time-insensitive transactions
    
*   For experiments or testing purposes
    

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/articles/understanding-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions#when-not-to-use-sub-1-sat-vb)

❌ When NOT to Use Sub-1 sat/vB:

*   Urgent transfers or large fund movements
    
*   Time-sensitive operations like snapshots, mints, or on-chain events
    
*   When generating a large number of small UTXOs, which could lead to future fee traps
    

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/articles/understanding-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions#best-practices)

🔧 Best Practices:

*   Only enable Sub-1 mode if you **fully understand the risks**
    
*   Always check the current **mempool conditions** before using low fees
    
*   Avoid merging multiple sub-1 UTXOs to prevent long-term fund lockups
    
*   Remember: if your sub-1 transaction gets stuck, accelerating it later can cost 20–200x more than the original fee
    

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/articles/understanding-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions#unisat-supports-sub-1-sat-vb-transactions)

UniSat Supports Sub-1 sat/vB Transactions

UniSat provides support for sub-1 fee transactions across several tools:

**✅ UniSat Inscribe**

When minting Ordinals or Runes, users can enable Sub-1 sat/vB Mode.

**✅ UniSat UTXO Management Tool on Bitcoin**

Perform UTXO management in Sub-1 sat/vB Mode:

*   Reclaim BTC trapped in useless inscription UTXOs
    
*   Batch send, one-click merge, split, lock, and unlock Odinals, Runes, Alkanes UTXOs
    
*   Check which UTXOs are currently locked in sub-1 sat/vB transactions
    

**✅ UniSat Wallet**

*   Save fees when sending BTC, Ordinals, Runes, and Alkanes
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/articles/understanding-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions#learn-more)

Learn More

To dive deeper into Sub-1 sat/vB transactions and risks, refer to our full guide: [https://docs.unisat.io/technical/understanding-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions/what-happens-when-bitcoin-fee-rates-drop-below-1-sat-vbarrow-up-right](https://docs.unisat.io/technical/understanding-sub-1-sat-vb-bitcoin-transactions/what-happens-when-bitcoin-fee-rates-drop-below-1-sat-vb)

# How to Transfer $BABY to a Cosmos Wallet | UniSat

If you previously used UniSat Wallet to participate in Babylon’s staking, you can transfer your $BABY airdrop to a Cosmos wallet for easier management and further operations.

This guide is for reference only. For more details about $BABY, please refer to the official Babylon website: [https://babylonlabs.io/arrow-up-right](https://babylonlabs.io/)

**Step 1: Prepare a Cosmos Wallet**

*   Choose a Cosmos-compatible wallet that supports $BABY, such as Leap or Keplr.
    
*   After creating your wallet account, switch the network to Babylon Network.
    
*   Click on Receive, and copy your BBN address.
    

(This example uses Leap wallet.)

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FHx0gxIc2otI8GCNQjlBe%252Fleap.gif%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D78a65b0d-96d0-4332-a36d-3adf73f0e00b&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=d3ec1fed&sv=2)

**Step 2: Open Your UniSat Wallet**

*   Open your UniSat Wallet, and switch to the **BTC Mainnet network**.
    
*   Go to the Discover page, and find the **Babylon** entry.
    

Ensure that your UniSat Extension Wallet is updated to the latest version v1.6.1. Click the link to download or update: [https://unisat.io/downloadarrow-up-right](https://unisat.io/download)

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FD8PQsKARKUmx9Oo7nlnm%252F1.PNG%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dcb5b0457-0e0c-4489-bf98-99e6f618e81b&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=d1b4500b&sv=2)

**Step 3: Go to the Babylon Page**

*   On the Babylon page, you will see the Claimed BABY section. Click the **Transfer** button in the Claimed BABY section.
    
*   Follow the on-screen prompts to click **Transfer $BABY to Cosmos Wallet**, then click **Confirm** to confirm your action.
    
*   In the transfer interface, input the BBN wallet address you created in Step 1 as the receiving address for your $BABY, and enter the transfer amount.
    
*   Once you confirm the information is correct, click Next, then sign the transaction to complete the transfer of your $BABY to your Cosmos wallet address.
    

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FcltHR24FOAXOJew3VMbG%252Fcosmos.gif%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dd7a258e4-160b-493a-91b9-7fa7860238e0&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=b63fbcea&sv=2)

**Additional Notes:**

*   Ensure that your Cosmos wallet is set up to support $BABY transfers and is connected to the Babylon Network.
    
*   If the Babylon DApp entry is not showing in your UniSat wallet, please ensure your wallet is updated to the latest version.
    
*   Babylon is a third-party project. Please make sure you fully understand the associated risks and terms before processing.
    
*   If you encounter any issues, please reach out to us via our Discord: [http://discord.gg/unisatarrow-up-right](http://discord.gg/unisat)
    

* * *

**FAQ**

**Q: I previously used UniSat Wallet to participate in Babylon BTC staking. How can I register for the BTC staking registration now?** A: The BTC staking registration on April 10 is only for addresses that participated in Babylon BTC Staking Phase Cap 1. If you used UniSat Wallet to stake BTC during Cap 1, you can go directly to the Babylon official website for more information.

If you participated in Babylon BTC staking Cap 2 or Cap 3, please stay tuned for future updates from the Babylon team.

* * *

**Q: When can I use UniSat Wallet to join Babylon Bitcoin Staking Phase 2?** A: Please stay tuned for more updates — we’ll keep you informed as soon as it’s live.

* * *

**Q: How do I access the Babylon website in UniSat Wallet?** A: Simply open the latest version of the UniSat Extension, go to Dapp Center, and tap on Babylon to jump straight to the site.

Download the latest UniSat Extension or update: [https://unisat.io/downloadarrow-up-right](https://unisat.io/download)

* * *

**Q: Can I convert my native $BABY token to BRC-20 BABY on Bitcoin via UniSat Wallet?** A: This feature is coming soon! Please stay tuned.

* * *

**Q: Why is the "My Staked BTC" amount displayed incorrectly on the UniSat wallet?** A: You can visit the [Babylon official websitearrow-up-right](https://babylonlabs.io/)
 to view the correct staked amount. This display issue will be fixed in the next version — thank you for your patience!

# InSwap on Fractal | UniSat

InSwap is the first open-source AMM DEX for Bitcoin-native assets, built natively on Bitcoin and Fractal.

It provides a seamless trading experience while maintaining the security standards of Bitcoin assets, enabling users to swap, provide liquidity, and earn native protocol assets across both networks without intermediaries

At the core of the service is a Bitcoin-native assets module that scales efficiently through rollups. Transactions are aggregated and batched using a novel sequencer which results in lower transaction costs and higher throughput capacity, enabling high-volume transactions directly on Bitcoin.

This document defines a Swap Module for Bitcoin-native assets.

Under the brc-20 Module, we introduce a mechanism that enables users to swap their balances within the module in a seamless and secure way.

All swap-related operations can be seen as a list, updated only by the module’s sequencer, and each event includes the signature of the initiating user.

This ensures maximum security and order throughout the swap process.This proposal defines two operations within the brc-20 module: commit and approve.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/inswap-on-fractal#swap-mechanism)

Swap Mechanism

Each module instance can include multiple swap pairs, and any user can publicly create a swap pair.

Each module operates independently, with the module’s sequencer responsible for aggregating (committing) all user activities internally and submitting them to the chain.

To prevent users from disrupting aggregation operations with unwrapping, balances in the module are split into two categories: fund balance and trade balance. wrapping into the module are credited to the trade balance, and only the trade balance can participate in aggregation operations.

Only the fund balance can be unwrapped. Users can use the approve operation to transfer the fund balance to the trade balance, or use the decreaseApproval function to convert the trade balance back into the fund balance. The approve inscription can be used to build a brc-20 market within the module.

When the sequencer sends the aggregated events inscription (commit), users will be charged an aggregation fee based on the number of events. The ticker used to pay the commit fee must be specified in the module initialization parameters, and only the fee ticker from the trade balance can be used to pay the commit fee.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/inswap-on-fractal#creating-a-new-swap-module-instance)

Creating a New Swap Module Instance

In the custom parameter section, the following must be set:

1.  Swap transaction fee rate
    
2.  Liquidity operation fee rate
    
3.  The ticker used to pay sequencer fees during aggregation
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/inswap-on-fractal#unwrapping-brc-20-ticker-from-the-module-to-a-target-address-unwrap)

Unwrapping brc-20 Ticker from the Module to a Target Address (Unwrap)

*   The user must first inscribe a unwrapping inscription, then transfer it to the target address for it to take effect. The inscription can only be used once.
    
*   The brc-20 tickers under the user’s account in the module will be unwrapping to the target address.
    
*   The inscription must include the module’s ID. If the module doesn’t exist, the unwrapping is invalid.
    
*   The module must be a white module for unwrapping to be supported. The unwrapping inscription does not lock the unwrapping balance when minted, but requires sufficient balance at the time of sending the unwrapping transaction. Unwrapping inscriptions sent back to the swap module will result in the destruction of the balance.
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/inswap-on-fractal#approving-brc-20-ticker-balances-in-the-module-to-a-target-address-approve)

Approving brc-20 Ticker Balances in the Module to a Target Address (Approve)

*   The user must first inscribe an Approve inscription, then transfer it to the target address for it to take effect. The inscription can only be used once.
    
*   The balance will be assigned to the authorized balance of the specified address in the module.
    
*   The inscription must include the module’s ID. If the module doesn’t exist, the approve inscription is invalid.
    
*   Only approved balances can be used in the commit event function. For safety, sequencers may reject user requests for approved balances that have fewer than 60 confirmations.
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/inswap-on-fractal#event-aggregation-in-swap)

Event Aggregation in Swap

All events that occur in the swap pool are described by functions. To ensure the orderliness of events, these functions are not inscribed individually but are placed in the module's aggregated inscription (commit).The basic rules are as follows:

*   During aggregation, each operation must be signed by the user’s address for all previous content (serialization including module and parent).
    
*   The aggregated inscription must be inscribed by the module sequencer and transferred to the module ID address to take effect. The sequencer is the address specified in the module inscription. The sequencer address can be updated using the update inscription.
    
*   For each function aggregated by the module sequencer, a fixed aggregation fee must be charged to the user. The user must wrap and approve sufficient fee assets in the module, or else the sequencer must reject the user’s event request. If the user has insufficient fees, the commit inscription will be invalid.
    

To avoid blocking when sending large numbers of commit inscriptions due to the mempool limit of 100KB and the 25-child transaction limit, commit inscriptions can initially be minted to the sequencer using unrelated UTXOs, regardless of the order. The sequencer can then periodically transfer commits in batches to the module address, ensuring that all previous logic is chained together and valid. This process significantly reduces the number of commit inscriptions that need to be transferred, minimizing the impact of the 25-child limit on the commit process.

**Aggregated Inscription (Commit)**

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/inswap-on-fractal#aggregated-inscription-structure-validity-details)

Aggregated Inscription Structure Validity Details

1.  Inscription field keys must be lowercase characters, and except for tick, values are case-sensitive.
    
2.  Duplicate fields are allowed, and extra fields are allowed.
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/inswap-on-fractal#user-signature-authorization)

User Signature Authorization

Each function in the aggregated inscription must include the user’s address and signature to authorize the sequencer to operate. Initially, only taproot address formats are supported, with other formats such as p2wpkh, p2wsh, p2sh, p2pkh, and hex-encoded arbitrary locking scripts to be supported later.The signature follows the BIP-322 format to sign the following content:

Each function has a function hashid, calculated as the SHA-256 hash of the serialized message (msg) with the following content:

Note: List the data for each field in the specified order, with each field ending in a newline character (`\n`).

Parameters in the params field are separated by spaces. If a field value is empty, omit that line in the serialized data.

The function ID is a fully computable intermediate result and it may be omitted from subsequent new inscriptions after testing is completed, meaning it does not need to be recorded again. However, it cannot be removed from inscriptions that have already been issued. The prevs field contains all function IDs submitted by the same user in the current inscription, sorted in the order in which the sequencer accepts them.

In the entire commit inscription, only the last signature for each address needs to be on-chain, as the intermediate function data has been overwritten by the last signature.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/inswap-on-fractal#swap-functions-available)

Swap Functions Available

**DeployPool**

*   Deploy a liquidity swap pool, specifying ticker0 and ticker1 as the two tickers participating in the swap pool. ticker0 and ticker1 must be different.
    
*   Only one liquidity pool is allowed to be deployed for the same pair of tickers within a module. There is no order relationship between the two tickers in the liquidity pool.
    
*   The liquidity ticker name will be "ticker0/ticker1". It is not possible to use liquidity tickers to deploy another liquidity pool.
    
*   Liquidity assets are always confined within the module they were deployed in and cannot be withdrawn. Each pool tracks the distribution of liquidity assets among holders.
    
*   Anyone can deploy a liquidity pool, but the deployer has no special permissions.
    

**AddLiquidity**

Users add liquidity, operating only on approved module balances.

**RemoveLiquidity**

Removes liquidity, with the tickers received belonging to the approved balance.

**Swap**

Executes a swap transaction, using only approved balances, with the received tickers belonging to the approved balance.

**DecreaseApproval**

Reduces the authorized balance of a ticker, increasing the withdrawable balance.

**Send**

Sends balances of various tickers within the module. Only authorized balances can be sent. The recipient’s balance will also be authorized. Liquidity assets cannot be sent.

**SendLp**

Sends liquidity tickers within the module.

**Function declaration**

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/inswap-on-fractal#swap-fees)

Swap Fees

Every swap incurs a 1.5% transaction fee. 1/6 of this fee goes to the platform, while the rest is distributed among liquidity providers (LPs).

Note: For example, if a user swaps 1000 ORDI for SATS, 1000 ORDI will be wrapped into the liquidity pool. A fee of 15 ORDI is deducted, so the actual amount of SATS the user receives is calculated based on 985 ORDI.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/inswap-on-fractal#network-fees)

Network Fees

The sequencer is responsible for gathering each aggregation function and minting the aggregated inscription on-chain, incurring network fees for miners to package the transaction. We calculate the network fee charged to users based on the current network fee rate and the user’s aggregation operations:

The formula: fee\=gasPricefee = gasPricefee\=gasPrice, where:

*   **gasPrice**: Network fee charged per function, depending on two factors: (a) the BTC network rate and (b)the market price of the ticker being charged:
    

gasPrice\=a/bgasPrice = a / bgasPrice\=a/b

*   **fee**: Measured in the ticker being charged. fee: Measured in the Tick being charged.
    

**Optimization of Function Bytes in Commit Inscription**

1.  Remove redundant function ID (saves 70 bytes)
    
2.  Only keep the last signature for the same address (saves 85 bytes)
    
3.  Number the address in the commit inscription and use the reference number in subsequent functions (saves 40 bytes)
    
4.  Reduce unnecessary precision in function parameter values, especially those far beyond slippage impact (saves 10 bytes)
    

The average size of a standard operation is 330 bytes. The theoretical maximum bytes that can be saved is 200 bytes.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/inswap-on-fractal#calculation-model)

Calculation Model

Using the existing Uniswap v2 model, we can define four operations for the pool.Given a swap pool with two tickers, ticker A and ticker B, the following notation is used:

*   A: The balance of ticker A in the pool.
    
*   B: The balance of ticker B in the pool.
    
*   C: The balance of liquidity tickers in the pool.
    

The constant product formula is:A⋅B\=kA \\cdot B = kA⋅B\=k, C\=A⋅B\=kC = \\sqrt{A \\cdot B} = \\sqrt{k}C\=A⋅B​\=k​

Four operations are as follows:

1.  **Swap ticker A for ticker B**: b\=a⋅Ba+Ab = \\frac{a \\cdot B}{a + A}b\=a+Aa⋅B​
    
2.  **Swap ticker B for ticker A**: a\=b⋅Ab+Ba= \\frac{b \\cdot A}{b + B}a\=b+Bb⋅A​
    
3.  **Add liquidity by adding ticker A and ticker B to receive liquidity ticker C:**
    

Use amount **a** and **b** to swap amount **c**, taking the smaller of the two: c\=aA⋅Cc = \\frac{a}{A}\\cdot Cc\=Aa​⋅C, c\=bB⋅Cc = \\frac{b}{B} \\cdot Cc\=Bb​⋅C

1.  **Remove liquidity by consuming liquidity assets to receive ticker A and ticker B:**
    

Use amount **c** to swap amounts **a** and **b**: a\=cC⋅Aa= \\frac{c}{C} \\cdot Aa\=Cc​⋅A , b\=cC⋅Bb = \\frac{c}{C} \\cdot Bb\=Cc​⋅B

The fee is deducted from the user’s tickers upfront.

During swap calculations, high-precision libraries are used to avoid precision loss during addition and multiplication. The final division will maintain the correct decimal precision for the ticker.

The user’s received amount will be the result of accurate calculations with truncated decimals. Manipulating precision for profit is not possible.

If the result is zero after truncation, the operation is not allowed, as the amount is too low.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/inswap-on-fractal#slippage)

Slippage

The slippage mechanism is similar to Uniswap, allowing users to tolerate a margin of error in the expected result, considering the following:

1.  Reduced Failure Rate: Front-running swap operations can fail due to concurrency. If a user’s signature takes 1 second and another user confirms their signature during that time, the transaction may fail. The longer the signature process, the higher the likelihood of failure.
    
2.  Lower Backend Pressure: Front-running swaps require frequent updates to swap data, increasing the backend query load.
    
3.  Uniswap-Consistent Model: Using the same model as Uniswap lowers the learning curve for users and increases adoption.
    

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/inswap-on-fractal#summary-of-swap-formulas)

Summary of Swap Formulas

**Slippage:**

*   exactIn: 1/(1+slippage)⋅quoteAmount1/(1+slippage) \\cdot quoteAmount1/(1+slippage)⋅quoteAmount
    
*   exactOut: (1+slippage)⋅quoteAmount(1+slippage) \\cdot quoteAmount(1+slippage)⋅quoteAmount
    

**Swap:**

*   amountIn: Input ticker amount
    
*   amountOut: Output ticker amount
    
*   reserveIn: Input ticker reserves in the pool
    
*   reserveOut: Output ticker reserves in the pool
    
*   Assume a 1.5% fee
    

**exactIn**

*   amountInWithFee\=amountIn⋅997amountInWithFee = amountIn \\cdot 997amountInWithFee\=amountIn⋅997
    
*   amountOut\=amountInWithFee⋅reserveOutreverseIn⋅1000+amountInWithFeeamountOut = \\frac{amountInWithFee \\cdot reserveOut }{reverseIn \\cdot 1000 + amountInWithFee} amountOut\=reverseIn⋅1000+amountInWithFeeamountInWithFee⋅reserveOut​
    

**exactOut**

*   amountIn \= reserveIn ⋅ amountOut ⋅ 1000 (reserveOut−amountOut) ⋅ 997  + 1amountIn = \\frac{reserveIn \\cdot amountOut \\cdot 1000 }{(reserveOut - amountOut) \\cdot 997}  + 1amountIn \= (reserveOut−amountOut) ⋅ 997reserveIn ⋅ amountOut ⋅ 1000 ​  + 1
    

**AddLiquidity:**

*   amount0: Amount of asset0 added
    
*   amount1: Amount of asset1 added
    
*   poolLp: LP asset supply in the pool
    
*   reserve0: Asset0 reserves in the pool
    
*   reserve1: Asset1 reserves in the pool
    
*   For the initial liquidity addition: lp\=amount0⋅amount1−1000lp = \\sqrt{amount0 \\cdot amount1} - 1000lp\=amount0⋅amount1​−1000
    
*   For subsequent liquidity additions: lp\=min⁡(amount0⋅poolLpreserve0,amount1⋅poolLpreserve1)lp = \\min(\\frac{amount0 \\cdot poolLp}{reserve0}, \\frac{amount1 \\cdot poolLp}{reserve1} ) lp\=min(reserve0amount0⋅poolLp​,reserve1amount1⋅poolLp​)
    

**RemoveLiquidity:**

*   Amount of asset0 received: amount0\=lp⋅reserve0poolLpamount0 = \\frac{lp \\cdot reserve0}{poolLp}amount0\=poolLplp⋅reserve0​
    
*   Amount of asset1 received: amount1\=lp⋅reserve1poolLpamount1 = \\frac{lp \\cdot reserve1}{poolLp}amount1\=poolLplp⋅reserve1​
    

**Platform Fee Calculation**

*   If the platform takes 1/6 of the fees, we need to calculate how much LP should be minted by the platform to capture exactly 1/6 of the incremental wealth.
    
*   Minting Timing: Before each liquidity addition/removal, the previously accumulated LP to be minted should be settled.
    
*   Assuming the platform collects 1/6 of the fees, it needs to calculate how much additional LP should be minted so that the platform's share is exactly 1/6 of the increment.
    
*   Timing of execution: Before each liquidity addition or removal, settle the cumulative LP amount that should be minted.
    
*   poolLp: LP asset supply in the pool
    
*   reserve0: Asset0 reserves in the pool
    
*   reserve1: Asset1 reserves in the pool
    
*   kLast: The k value calculated after the last liquidity event
    
*   The square root of the current assets in the pool: rootK\=reserve0⋅reserve1rootK = \\sqrt{reserve0 \\cdot reserve1}rootK\=reserve0⋅reserve1​
    
*   The square root of the last liquidity event: rootKLast\=kLastrootKLast = \\sqrt{kLast}rootKLast\=kLast​
    
*   Platform lp amount: lp\=poolLp⋅(rootK−rootKLast)rootK⋅5+rootKLastlp = \\frac{poolLp \\cdot (rootK - rootKLast)}{rootK \\cdot 5 + rootKLast } lp\=rootK⋅5+rootKLastpoolLp⋅(rootK−rootKLast)​
    

**The derivation process is shown below:**

![](https://docs.unisat.io/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3523236551-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252FJ4NHAHIVnWQiEecvs1By%252Fuploads%252FDypFSpIJ7GVEEAJ1HlTz%252F1.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D7134f205-7064-4b19-9ae7-797599736d42&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=d245ed7f&sv=2)

As shown above, to achieve 1/6 of the new wealth, the minted LP should satisfy the following equation: lplpSupply\=∆/6(∆5/6)+rootKLast\\frac{lp}{lpSupply} = \\frac{∆/6}{(∆5/6) + rootKLast }lpSupplylp​\=(∆5/6)+rootKLast∆/6​, where _∆ = rootK - rootKLast_

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/fractal-bitcoin/inswap-on-fractal#faq)

FAQ

**Can anyone deploy a swap module?**

*   Yes, anyone can deploy a swap module, but managing it requires some complexity:
    
    *   You need to provide an API for users to query the current pool and submit new transactions.
        
    *   You must regularly mint inscriptions to submit transactions on-chain.
        
    
*   UniSat will parse all swap transactions on-chain.
    
*   app-swap.unisat.io is a product of UniSat, where UniSat has deployed a series of trading pair pools for users to participate in swaps.

      "p": "brc20-module",

# brc20-swap Early Access | UniSat

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.unisat.io/misc/events/brc20-swap-early-access#the-criteria)

the criteria

*   Active community members who have traded at least 1 BTC on the UniSat Marketplace between July 16th and September 20th
    
*   Active community members who have accumulated at least 500 UniSat Points through UniSat Inscribe between July 16th and September 20th
    
*   OG PASS holders (at block height 808,559)

# UniSat OG Pass Collection | UniSat

The UniSat OG pass is a commemorative card distributed for free to early supporters. It currently grants the following benefits:

*   A 15% reduction in UniSat Inscribing service fees.
    
*   A 25% reduction in UniSat Marketplace service fees.
    

####

Email Protection
